  135. First off I have to say I was able to purchase this from Amazon for $29.99, which informs heavily on the value score. A long-time owner of two consecutive Braun 8k/9k systems, here is what you get. There are no quality nor perk frills here, this is about as spartan as it gets- no stands, no little bag, no cleaning system. The Remington is lightweight and not well balanced. Despite largely plastic construction, it looks less assuming or intrusive in the bathroom than the Braun in its mountain stand or any Panasonic with their loud colors and chrome; however, those others come with stands and the Remington could really use a stand. This unit is loud, which is not an auditory concern so much a reflection of overall quality. Like so many other shavers nowadays, this one features incredibly bright and annoying dancing LED lights, because the power status of your shaver is definitely something you need shoved down your throat when you visit the bathroom at 3 a.m. Shaving performance is good, I have pretty easy demands; heartier or more complex hairs may demand more. My travel Panasonic does substantially better primarily because it has a faster motor, but this does the job as well as my Braun ever did and I do not feel I need to save more time on my shave. The foils are wider than I am used to, makes it hard but not impossible to negotiate the soul patch. The pushbutton power button took some getting used to and I have accidentally shut it off a couple of times; it feels like something that could break eventually. Overall, the unit feels fragile, I would hesitate to use this as a travel razor without some substantial protection added. The verdict? Probably did not sound that great above, but at thirty bucks this is a steal. Fact is, a large number of people are dissatisfied with their razors costing 5-7x this one. If this unit failed in one year, I probably got my money's worth. I did not buy a razor to be quiet or to come up with clever ways to clean it. This one simply does its job as asked.

  302. This is the first Remington razor i have ever used. My experiences have always been with the triple-head Norelco. I will make some comparisons here, since if I were thinking about trying a the Remington, i’d probably want to know how it worked compared to my own razor. It is definitely a different experience, however not altogether a bad one..<br /><br />The shaver fits comfortably in my hand, which is probably a bit bigger than normal. Everything about the design seems proper and efficient; the weight distribution, the angles, the charging mechanisms, etc. But there are differences with the business end of it..<br /><br />The razor came with a full charge, and the easy-to-see LEDs light up indicating how much charge remains. It never moved off full, so I cannot evaluate the battery life. Cleaning is easy; just remove the cover around the cutters and blow or rinse it out. No issue there. I did not rinse the shaver to clean it, i just blew it clean.<br /><br />It sounds different than the Norelco, probably a bit noisier, but not offensive. It sounds more like barber’s cutters.<br /><br />I usually go 3-5 days between shaves. I rarely shave everyday, so there is always a bit of stubble for the razor to handle. A couple times during this review period i went longer, sometimes shorter. I never shave every day, consistently, so I am reviewing the razor on how it behaved in my normal mode of operation.<br /><br />After the first 5 day shave, the first thing i noticed was that the Remington shaver has more &#34;pull&#34; to it; that is, I experience some discomfort as I'm shaving with it. The Norelco has no noticeable pulling after 5 days. This is not a big deal for me, but it might be for some. I shaved half my face with each machine. The Norelco did a quicker job, with less discomfort. I had to go over the areas with the Remington 2-3 times before it felt smooth. It always seemed to me that the Remington screen system and it’s basically rectangular shaving contact area would be a better choice for areas like the neck. But after using it, this does not seem to be the case. The Norelco did a better and faster job all over, and just seemed to cut better than the Remington. This was especially the case when i went a full week between shaves. The Remington seemed to have problems handling the longer beard, and i had to retrace several times to get a smooth shave. The Norelco, (with cutters over a year old, I just realized) handled the beard much better in my judgement. The mistake I used to make was to push harder the longer the beard was, but i have since learned they all seem to cut better with very little pressure. Even so, the Remington just didn’t cut as well; the Norelco cuts down my long beard very quickly, and leaves very little need for a second go-around. It took noticeably longer to shave the 7-day beard with the Remington. However, the overall result was still a very close shave.<br /><br />The razor handled a short, daily shave much better. The times i shaved several days in a row, there was little or no difference between the machines. It shaved very close, and did so on the first time around.<br /><br />So, overall, if shaving time is not a concern for you, and you are not bothered by a noticeable “pull” on the long beard, or if you if you use the shaver like my father does—twice a day—you will probably have no issues with the Remington.ar shaving contact area would be a better choice for areas like the neck.   311. Ever since a traffic accident left me rather gun-shy about using razor blades on my face, I've been an electric shaver user. I still have my old Norelco (the thing is almost 40 years old!) and would probably still be using that but they don't make replacement heads for it anymore.<br /><br />So I transitioned to the foil shavers and found them to be mediocre, but useful enough to keep the undergrowth trimmed back until the gardeners could come in once a week and do a proper job (AKA using a razor only once a week instead of every day). And for a couple of decades, this was my usual routine. The foil shavers never lasted more than a year or two before the foil heads wore through and often times, finding replacement heads was impossible. I have a drawer of perfectly good, if worn, foil shavers hoping one day I'll be able to find a screen or cutter for them. And because of their lack of longevity, I've rarely spent very much on them (which, admittedly, might have something to do with why they're not lasting very long).<br /><br />So when my last foil shaver wore through (always an exciting feeling to have one's skin abraded away in an instant and foofing the cat's tail by suddenly howling in pain), and I couldn't find any replacement screens or cutters for it, I was getting annoyed and decided to go a bit higher end. Most of the shavers I got before were in the 15-20 dollar range. I figured I'd go about double and see if there was something worthy of abrading my face in the (hopefully more distant than usual) future. (Note: I got this under Amazon Prime at the time at a lower price than it's listed now and would likely not have spent the money to get it at the price showing for it as of January 27, 2015)<br /><br />Thus far, I've found it to be a pretty good shaver. It has most of the cutting power of a razor without the drawbacks of a conventional foil shaver. Most foil shavers I've used leave a few hairs uncut which, after a few days, get too long to ever cut with a foil head. That's why I occasionally used a blade - to get the last hairs standing. But this shaver has a little lawn trimmer built into the head between the foils that trims down these standers to a level where the foil head can handle.<br /><br />This means, for a foil head, it's the best shave I've ever had. Blades will get closer, but not by a lot. And I haven't had to USE a blade since I got it.<br /><br />Bonus.<br /><br />So for allowing me to put away the twin blades of death, this little (or not so little) shaver has earned my respect as a credible, front-line, handle-it-all shaver on par with my trusty Norelco. My only concern is its longevity, which might take a star off if it isn't at least as durable as the cheaper models. The cost/benefit ratio of buying another one of these, and buying more razors will factor into whether or not I get replacement heads for it (something I checked to see if they had before buying) or go back to something cheaper and buy cheap razors for the standing hairs again.<br /><br />So my five star rating is on the assumption that the foils will last at least as long as they do in the cheaper models (and hopefully longer!) because otherwise it gives an excellent shave.<br /><br />I usually gush over my five star ratings, and I'd be doing it over this, but I don't know about longevity. The current price would make me hesitate about getting another one if the foil doesn't last substantially longer than the less expensive ones and/or if the price of head replacements has gone up as well. I'm always cost-conscious (I'm a cheap SOB), so value to me means excellent performance for the value. The performance IS excellent. The value remains to be seen.<br /><br />However, if the price comes down to about double the legal drinking age, get it if you need one. At that price, it's definitely worth it.t with a foil head. There is a major price difference between the two units – nearly $50 difference. However, I will use a razor for several years before buying another. My last Braun (505) lasted nearly five years without even trading out the cutting block and foil.   693. This is a very good shaver, at least for me. Just some history, I have been shaving with electric shavers for 40 years. When I tried using a blade, I would end up with little spots of blood all over my neck and jaw. If I go without shaving for several days, then I might be able to get away with using a blade without too much of a problem. So, I began using an electric and have been happy with most of them. My last electric shaver was a Braun model 5614, dual foil with a center cutter for longer hairs. I have been using it for the last 17 years and have been mostly happy with it but, it is getting old, the battery doesn't hold a charge as long as it used to and it will be just a matter of time before I can't get blades for it. What I need from an electric shaver is to be able to use it with or without a cord. That way if the battery fails, I can still shave with it. The F5 seems to be the only Remington model with this feature. With the Braun, as soon as the battery charge ran out, I could just plug it in and finish my shave, then leave it plugged in until fully charged. It also need to give a relatively quick and comfortable shave and be reasonably priced. However, when shopping around for another razor, I decided I might want to try another brand. I looked at Brauns but the reviews didn't seem to be as good as I would have expected considering the good experience I have had with mine. It seems todays razors don't match up to the quality and performance of the older ones. Then, I saw the Remington F5-5800 and saw that it had fairly good reviews and decided to give it a try. So now the review....... I have been using the Remington for about 6 weeks now. Comparing the Remington to the Braun, I immediately noticed it was a little bigger than the Braun overall and the shaving head was also a little bigger but it still felt comfortable in my hand and I could maneuver it without any problems. The shaver came partially charged but I still followed the instructions and charged it for 24 hours before using it. Using it, it seems to have a pretty powerful motor. If I tried to shave with the braun with 3 days growth, the motor would bog down a little but not with the Remington. It stays at the same rpm's no matter what. As with all electric razors I have used, I still have to go over the same area multiple times to get it as close as I can get it, especially around the neck area. It seems that much hasn't changed about electric razors over the years. As with any new razor, it takes time for your face to adjust to it. However, after 6 weeks, my face still gets a little sore using this razor. If you look at the attached photos, you can see that the foil head protrudes more and there is more space between the foils and the center cutter than on the Braun. My only conclusion was that since the center cutter was more exposed to the face, it may be scraping the skin more so than the Braun did. The Remington did do a very good job shaving, though and am happy with the results. I probably got about a dozen shaves, shaving every other day on average before I had to recharge it. It did run out while I was shaving, so I just plugged it in and finished my shave.The Braun would give me maybe 4-5 shaves before the battery went dead. But, after 17 years, I would expect that. The one thing I did notice on the Remington was that it still seemed to run at full rpm right up until the battery went dead. The motor on the braun would slowly fade away until it would finally stop. The Remington only took a few hours to fully charge it. I like the battery indicator lights showing the level of the charge, but noticed it would still give me like 5-6 more shaves even after the bottom red light would be on. The one feature I cannot review is the pop up trimmer. I did not use the trimmer and really have no need for a it since I don't have a beard or mustache and I just use a regular blade to trim my sideburns. Cleaning is easy. Just grab the front and back of the shaver foil head where the ridges are with your thumb and forefinger and give a solid pull and it will pop right off. You can either run it under water or use the included brush to clean it. Place the foil head back in place and snap it in and you're done. I gave it 4 stars instead of 5 because it wasn't as comfortable of a shave as my Braun but was acceptable and the shave wasn't as quick as I had hoped for but it did a better overall job. If it wasn't for those two issues, I would have given it 5 stars. I cannot comment on how long the cutters and foil last but after 6 weeks and probably 17-18 shaves, the shaver still seems to cut as close as it did when it was new, as I would expect it to. This is just my opinion and results may vary but I can recommend it. ****EDITED 1/4/15**** After about another month of shaving with this razor, I decided to return it. Having sensitive skin, it was more rough on my skin than my Braun, and I wasn't willing to deal with that. Also, a couple of times because the center cutter is more exposed, I could feel it \\"nipping\\" at the edge of my lip. It didn't cut the lip but it made me more cautious while shaving around that area. Another thing was with the charge indicator lights. It seems after only a few shaves once the shaver has been fully charged, the indicator lights start to move rather quickly to the last red light, so I was never completely sure how much of a charge it still had. The closeness of the shave was still good, however, and the price is certainly reasonable so I leave the star rating at 4. If Remington can redesign the cutting head so the foils are closer to the center cutter and tweaks the indicator lights so it shows a more accurate indication as to the battery level, I may try this shaver again.

  794. This shaver is an updated model to the Remington MS2-390 shaver. I have to say it is not much of an update. This shaver does a very good job of getting a close shave. Perhaps the same results as the expensive Braun Series 7 but at a fraction of the cost. However, the only drawback I see in this newer model is with the interceptor or what I will call the middle trimmer. The MS2-390 had a pop up trimmer that was the same length of the foils. Instead of having a trimmer in the middle of the two foils like this model, it would pop up to one of the sides of the foil. This design made it perfect for edging up side burns and trimming longer facial hairs. This model attempts the same concept, that the trimmer in the middle of the foils (interceptor) does the same thing. The difference is when the trimmer was on the side, you could adjust the angle of your razor and comb up those longer hairs to be shaved by the trimmer. With the way this feature is now, you have to always keep your razor at a 90 degree angle so that the interceptor can make contact with your face. With no way to adjust the angle of the interceptor because of the two foils, it misses patches of neck hair. Regardless of this personal flaw for me. The razor does perform very well. I own a Braun Series 7 and aside from missing the cleaning station, this razor is on par with that razor. So if you are debating about getting a new shaver, try this one first before you lay down some hard earned cash on a Braun Series 7. Just beware if you have facial hair that grows in all directions, you may want to get a fine beard trimmer for those few missing hairs this razor now leaves behind.

  829. This replaces an older model Remington MS2-390 I've been using for five years. The old one had gotten to the point where the battery only held a charge for about two days. This F5-5800A still uses a NiMH battery, but it seems like it holds a charge for longer (and doesn't drain as much idle) than the MS2-390 did. The battery display is handy for knowing exactly how much power you have left, which I like, because the other one died pretty suddenly when it was low.<br /><br />Between the foils on this shaver is the &#34;Intercept&#34; central shaver, which actually does improve the shave. I've had times where you miss a hair one or two days and suddenly it's too long for the foil to pick up, this central blade shortens those nicely so the foils can grab them.<br /><br />The one part I don't like is the detail trimmer. It seems like most manufacturers like using these flip-up style ones. You can only use them in one direction otherwise the friction of moving the shaver causes the flipout to close. The other model MS2-390 had a far superior mechanism - it popped up vertically and was rigid no matter which way you applied it to your face. That's the one thing I miss from the other model.
